4.7.5 Contingence Analysis
The project-related contingences include the leakage of poisonous, harnful, inflammable and
explosive matters during transportation and traffic accidents of vehicles transporting
aforementioned matters. The contingences occur seldom will cause unexpected damage to the
environment.
a) Impact analysis of contingences
The leakage may occur during the transportation or be resulted from the traffic accident. The
leaked liquid matter may permeate into the urban sewage network and subsequently pollute
the rivers such as Yunliang River and South Shahe River or, if it is inflammable or explosive
matter, explosion of urban drainage pipeline may be caused. The volatile matters may diffuse
in the air and form air pollution. The traffic accident will cause traffic jams in some road
sections which will subsequently deteriorate the ambient air quality. Besides, the fire and
explosion resulted from the traffic accident will also cause air pollution.
According to the estimation, the leaked polluant (e.g. the poisonous, inflammble and
explosive acrylonitrile) will pollute the leeward segmental area of 800 m, given that the
stability of atmosphere is D Class and the ground wind velosity is 2.0 m/s. The segmental
area includes 0.043 km2 of high-density polluant area (1000 mg/m3), 0.055 km 2 of medium-
density polluant area (500 mg/mr3) and 0.069 km2 of low-density polluant area (300 mg/m3).
The boundaries of these three areas is 420 m and 610 m from the polluting source in the
leeward direction. When all the polluant leaks out due to traffic accident, the polluting range
will be greatly enlarged.
b) Precautions against contingences and handling measures
(1) As the proposed road is located in densely populated urban area, it should be closed to
vehicles transporting dangerous goods.
(2) The companies who have to transport dangerous goods on proposed road must get the
permit for transporting issued by traffic administration authority. and the vehicles transporting
dangerous goods shall travel on designated routes, lanes and at designated speed and time.
Besides, the vehicles and containers must comform to the relevant technical standards.
(3) The traffic administration and the motor vehicles maintenance shall be intensified, and
motor vehicles drivers shall be trained to minimize the occurrance of traffic accident.
(4) Great attention shall be attached to design of bridges and strict construction supervision
and acceptance shall be carried out. Maintenance rules of bridge shall be made out to zero the
possibility of bridge collapse.
(5) Once the leakage of dangerous goods takes place. traffic policeman team. fire-fighting
team etc. shall go to the accident site in time and take emergency measures. e.g.. absorb.
collect. dilute or cover the leakage. to prevent the diffusion of polluant. Further measures
shall also be taken to eliminate the adverse impact on environment.
(6) The traffic administration authlority shall disperse the vehicles and people on accident site
115



Liaoning Urban Transport Project-Anshan Subproject       Environmental Impact Assessment
in time. clear up the barriers on road and mend the damaged bridge and road in order to
resume the traffic as soon as possible.
4.8 Alternatives
4.8.1 General
Four alternatives related to different road sections are as follows (see Fig.2-3 for details):
* Alternative A
An elevated road from new Wuyi Road to the entrance of Laodong Road shall be setup at the
west side of north section of Jianguo Road instead of surface widening of north section of
Jianguo Road, and the existing north section of Jianguo Road can be used as special road for
passenger traffic.
* Alternative B
The existing Shahe Street at north side of Hebei Road (recommended by the preferred
alignment) shall be reconstructed instead of building Hebei Road.
* Alternative C
The road across Zhendong Metal Structure Factory shall run along the south side of the plant
area.
* Alternative D
According to the size recommended by the preferred alignment, a bridge shall be built across
Shahe River at the west side of the existing Laodong Bridge which shall be used only for
traffic of non-motor vehicles from south to north.
4.8.2 Noise and Vibration
4.8.2.1 Noise
a) Analysis of noise pollution of alternatives
Compared to the preferred alignment, the alternatives B, C and D of Hebei Road, South Ring
Road and Laodong Bridge show only slight change of construction site and the design
parameter of the road, the motor vehicle flow etc. are almost the same. The acoustic
environment along the road according to alternatives is similar with the prediction in
paragraph 4.2 of this report, so no further indication of noise impact is necessary.
The elevated road in alternative A is proposed to set up at the west side of the existing
Jianguo Road. The side of the elevated road is over 50 m away from the first row of buildings
of sensitive area. Compared to surface widening of ground road (preferred alignment ). the
alternative A will be different in the acoustic environment along the line.
b) Comparison of acoustic environment quality between alternative A and the preferred
alignment
Greater noise shall occur when motor vehicles run fast on elevated road and the noise is more
complicated. Because the proposed elevated road shall be far from sensitive area and medium
high or lower buildings shall be mainly built in the sensitive area, so the prediction points of
noise within sensitive area shall be set on the ground surface. The noise prediction value of

the elevated road alternative is the result of noise of motor vehicles running on the elevated
road plus that on the ground road (existing Jianguo Road ). The result of prediction is shown
in Table 4-45.
In order to make the noise predication value of the alternatives and the preferred alignment
comparable, the noise prediction points 0 m, 10 m, 20 m, 30 m, 50 m and 100 m from red line
bf Jianguo Road are 50 m, 60 m. 70 m, 80 m, 100 m and 150 m away from the side of the
elevated road. The predication results of acoustic enviromnent quality in 2010 of elevated
road alternative and ground road widening conception are shown in Table 4-45.

4.8.2.2 Vibration
In the altematives B. C. and D. the vibration shall not be increased. Though the vibration
caused by the running vehicle on the elevated road of alternative A is greater than that on the
ground road. it will have much less impact on people's health. The vibration shall fall down
rapidly as distance increases. because the elevated road is far away from sensitive area.
Therefore. the phenomenon of 'ibration disturbance to people of the alternatives shall be
similar with that of the preferred alignment.

4.8.4 Soil and Vegetation
4.8.4.1 Analysis of Impact on Soil and Vegetation
Through the site investigation of 4 altermatives recommended in the design, the impact of
alternatives on the soil and vegetation isn't higher than that of the preferred alignment. The
impact changes of alternatives are analyzed as follows:
a) Alternative A
To build the elevated road, 126 poplars, 551 willow-s ( 55°o big trees ), 281 small pines. 451
small peach trees and 70 other small trees will be cut down. That is to say that a total green
area of 12195 m2 will be damaged. Compared with the corresponding road sections of the
preferred alignment, 1344 trees will be saved. In the meantime, because this section of
Jianguo Road will no be widened, near 10900 m2 of planted area and greensward will not be
occupied. In addition, after the change of the tram line, a part of land occupied by the original
line will be greened. i.e. additional 7200 m2 of green area can be achieved in comparison with
the preferred alignment.
b) Alternative B
This alternative will widen the newly-built Shahe Road. so having no impact on soil and
118



Liaoning Urban Transport Project-Anshan Subproject                 Environmental Impact Assessment
vegetation. Conversely, because Hebei  Road will not be built, 12600 m2 farm land shall be
free from occupation and 232 trees from cutting down ( green area 2948.8 mi2).
c) Alternative C
This alternative will make the newly built section of South Ring Road across the farm land at
the South of Anshan Zhendong Metal Structure Factory instead of crossing the factory. In this
case, 2190 m2 more farm land shall be occupied. At the same time, considering the planting
on both sides of this road and using separation belt for greening, we can plant 24 trees and
obtain 20 M2 lawn more than the preferred aligniment.
d) Alternative D
This alternative will build a new bridge at west side of existing Laodong Bridge. In this case,
400 m2 more vegetation land will be occupied and 20 more trees will be cut.

4.8.5 Surface Water
Among all the altemative,s of this project, only the impact on surface water of alternative D is
a little different from that of preferred alignment. According to the preferred alignment the
old bridge shall be demolished. some suspended solid occur and get into South Shahe River.
In altemative D, since the old bridge will not be demolished, the total amount of suspended
solid into South Shahe River is similar to that in preferred alignment in which a new bridge
will be built. Since the construction phase of demolishing the old bridge is relatively short. so
the relevant pollution will have little impact on South Shahe River which is only used for
irrigation.

addition, displacement of Shahe Village will be avoided and expense of constructing Hebei
Road will be canceled. In this assessment, alternative B has significant effect on protecting
cultivated land, minifying displacement and so on. so we suggest to utilize alternative B
instead of utilizing Hebei Road new construction conception.

5 PLAN OF ENVIRONMENT MONITORING AND
MANAGEMENT
5.1 Institution and Staff Training
5.1.1 Establishment of Institution
The project shall be managed successively by ARPO during the phase of construction and by
Anshan Urban Construction Administration Bureau after its completion. Both institutions
known as administrative institutes shall provide full-time environmental protection staff.
The administrative institutions shall be staffed by one or two full-time environmental
protection personnel to ensure the responsibility of daily management, accepting complaints
concerning environrnental impact, handling pollution cases as well as controlling and
coordinating the monitoring activities on motor vehicles emission and traffic noise which are
conducted by Anshan Environment Monitoring Center and Anshan Vehicle Inspecting
Station.
The relation among organizations of environmental management and environment monitoring

The responsibilities of the institutions shown above are to guarantee that the project attain the
requirements of environmental protection, the AEPB is the government organization in
charge of the environmental protection. The environmental management, monitoring and
counseling etc. in are of great importance to the project as the weak link of the environmental
protection of the project is that of construction phase.
The construction company must strengthen the environmental protection. Each construction
company shall be staffed with at least one full-time environmental protection engineer who
shall be in charge of the prevention and handling of environmental pollution and the technical
instruction on the construction personnel. The AEPB shall send supervisors to give the
construction company instruction and handle the pollution cases in time. Should any
environmental pollution or disputes relating to the environmental pollution occur. the
victimized party can file the complaint to the local departments in charge of the
environrmental protection.
At least two employees of each construction company shall attend the environmental
protection training, refer to Table 5-1 about the training content and duration.

management of the environmental protection of the project.
The environmental protection work in operational phase including mainly of the
implementation of the mitigation measures and maintenance of noise reducing facilities shall
be undertaken by the project office and supervised by the AEPB. The environmental
monitoring in operational phase shall be undertaken by the AEMC.

-5.1.2 Responsibilities of Administrative Institutions
The Administrative Institutions of JRR shall not only conduct realization of the project,
maintenance of road facilities, but also have the following environmental responsibilities:
*   Execute routine monitoring on motor vehicle enmissions. traffic noise and vibration.
* Make inspection tour to construction site to offer advice on environrnental problems and
to supervise that the construction contractors 'follow the state and local rules of
environmental protection in construction phase.
*   Help Anshan Environmental Protection Bureau (AEPB) to handle traffic accidents
related to pollution.
*   Receive complaints from  residents. enterprises & institutions and assist AEPB to solve
such problems.
*   Assist AEPB to offer trainino to project contractors.
*   Review monitoring results and make appropriate decisions tor mitigation if needed.

5.3 Environmental Action Plan
The Environmental Action Plan provides mitigation measures and scope of environmental
management and monitoring during the construction and operational phase. The purpose of
EAP is to ensure successful implementation of mitigation measures. Realization of EPA will
reasonably improve the environmental quality of areas related to the project.
The EAP has the following roles:
3   Ensure the mitigating measures be implemented.
*   Provide implementation documents.
-   Ensure the responsibility and role of administrative institutions be fulfilled.
*   Define the environmental monitoring range in construction and operational phase.
*   Ensure the funds for environmental protection be available.
EAP is one of the important documents that will be submitted to the World Bank for project
approval. For details see EAP report.

6 PUBLIC PARTICIPATION
6.1 Aim and Significance of Public Participation
The aim of public participation is to know the public suggestion and demands to the project
and submit these suggestions to the departments concerned for study and consultation in order
to make public conforn the project completely. and the public participation will play an
important role in taking effective measures and making decisions for the project construction,
therefore the comprehensive and long-time benefit of the project will be gained.
6.2 Mode and Content of Public Participation
In the first phase of public participation, the project environment assessment team held
meeting to collect the public opinions. issued list of inquiry and made random investigation to
learn the public suggestions and opinions to the proposed project. After the measures made by
the assessment team had been adopted. the second public investigation was conducted again
to seek public suggestions to these measures.
The content of the first investigation:
a) Beneficial or harmful, long term or short term. acceptable or unacceptable impact of the
proposed project to the people during the construction and operational phase of the project.
b) The attitude or demands and specific suggestions to the project from the public, enterprises
and institutions impacted by the proposed project.
6.3 General Investigation of Public Participation
In order that the investigation of public participation can really reflect public suggestions to
the whole proposed project and that the investigated objects can fully represent all aspects,
the environment assessment team held meeting to seek public suggestions to traffic road
reconstruction on December 2 to December 15 in 1996 and along both sides of the road
proposed to be constructed in Tiedong, Tiexi and Lishan Districts, Shahe and Houyu villages
which shall be affected by the project. The minutes of meeting were taken and the list of
inquiry was distributed to the impacted individuals within above impacted areas and the
investigated members are selected at random among the public for detail investigation. The
investigated public are from different trades and professions and represent different social
strata and aspects. 456 persons of different age. sex. profession and title were investigated.
The detail is shown in Table 6-1.
After having discussed methods and measures to deal with the suggestions and opinions
which  had been proposed in thc first investigation wNith Anshan Construction Committee.
ARPO. Anshan Town &  CouLntrV Constructioni P'lanninig Institute, Beijing Municipal
Engineering Design & Researchi Institute. the EA tcauim conducted the second investigation
among people who had proposLd suggestions in the first in% estigation on March 3 to 12. 1997.
The EA team introduced solutioll to their suggestioni and collected their feedback.
In addition. 68 persons ha\e been investigated on Nlar. 2 and Mar.3 to collect their

suggestions and opinions tO the hLild-up of nexx depoIts and the engineering of Hongqi Road
reconstruction.

6.4 First Public Participation and Investigation Result
From the public investigation. it is known that most of the people. enterprises and institutions
are for the project. Among 456 persons, 96.24 percent are for the project, 1.31 percent are
against the project, 2.45 percent adopt indifferent attitude. and 57.24 percent of 456 persons
put forward their opinions and suggestions to the project which focus on noise disturbance
and inconvenience of crossing street. All the enterprises and institutions investigated are for
the project.
In addition. most people investigated agree with the build-up of new bus depots and the
engineering of Hongqi Road reconstruction. All the people support the reconstruction
engineering and even hope the early starting of the enginieering.
6.5 Opinions and Demands of Public to the Project
From investigation of public participation we can know that although most of public are for
this project, they give maximum attention to these problems related to their own benefit and
caused by the project, such as noise pollution, greenery patches occupancy, the problem of
crossing street and displacement arrangement, therefore they put forward the following
suggestions and demands.
a) 3-6-2 section of Jianguo Road
Sifangtai Fruits Wholesale Market. one of the biggest markets in North-east region of China,
lies at the west side of the road. Every day, almost 500 motor vehicles, 3000 man-power
vehicles, and almost 50 thousand people come in and out this market. So left-turning problem
for those vehicles should be solved.
b) 1-2-1 section of Zhonghua Road
The east side of the road is against Nanchangdian Primary School. Although the school
supports the road widening construction. they ask for taking noise control measures.
132



Liaoning Urban Transport Project-Anshan Subproject        Environmental Impact Assessment
c) 2-3-1 section of Yongchang Street
Wuyi Road Primary School lies to the south side of this road section. After Yongchang Street
is widened, Sandaojie Clothing. Shoes and Cap Street ( Bagua clothing market ) and Erdaojie
Vegetable Market will be divided into two parts. so the school and the peddlers ask for
solving problem of pedestrians crossing street, in addition. both sides of the road shall be very
close to the residential buildings and Wuyi Road Primary School. Some existing buildings are
within the red line. the residents and school give strong response to the traffic noise and ask
for taking measures to reduce noise.
d) 2-3-2 section of Yongchang Street
People's Park, Ng jS Middle School and Gangdu Primary School of Anshan lie to the north
of this road section, populous residential area lies to the south side, and more old people (879
persons are over 55 years old) are living there, therefore, safety measures for crossing street
are requested.
e) 3-5-2 section of Jianguo Road
The office of the recreational place-Anshan Old People's Palace, is located on the side of the
road section, so noise mitigation measures must be taken.
f) 3-2-3 section of Jianguo Road
Lishan Wholesale Market and L.aodong Road Primary School are located on the west side of
this road section. so measures for crossing street must be taken.
g) 2-1-3 section of Huangang Road
Qianjin Primary School must be moved in order to construct this road section. By
interviewing and investigating. it is known that because this primary school is impacted
heavily by the vibrating and noise of AISC and its special railway line, most pupils in this
area went to schools in other areas. To displace the schiool is popular confidence.
h)The only existing greenery patches and trees must be protected during the construction
phase of the project.

By the set.ond social interview, ing and investigating along each section of the project road. the

satisfied yet.

7 CONCLUSIONS
7.1 Comparison of With and Without JRR in 2010
The negative impact of traffic noise with JRR on the other roads within the urban area is
slightly lower than without JRR.
With JRR, the total emission of CO, NOx, N02 and HC from vehicles in the whole city is less
23.36%, 17.86%. 17.86% and 21.72% respectively than that of without JRR.
With JRR, at road sections to the south of Wuyi Road Interchange, the contribution volume
of emission from vehicles to air environmnent is small: under the condition of south or west
wind, it is less thanAwithout JRR at the north section of Jianguo Road and at the east-west
road of the project; under the conditions of other wind directions, it is slightly higher than
without JRR, but the absolute total emission under latter wind direction is less than that under
the former wind directions.
With JRR, the negative impact on foot travelers and AISC's (Anshan Iron & Steel Complex)
production & staff transportation is less than without JRR.
The JRR project has significant importance for inhibiting further deterioration of Anshan air
environrment, but also a little negative impact in the view of traffic noise and pedestrians
walking at somc sections.
7.2 Positive Impact
Relieve traffic pressure of other trunk roads in Anshan City. Solve the problem of traffic jam
of AISC's production & staff transportation, reduce traffic load near area of railway station,
thoroughly eliminate the conftusion and crowded situation of Anshan urban traffic.
Shorten the time and distance of traveling of pedestrians and motor & motorless vehicles,
favorable to improve the life quality of public.
Arrange the resettled residents in the neighborhood and incorporate the dismantled enterprises
into the appropriate industrial zones, to improve living environment of displaced residents.
make the city arrangement more reasonable and raise the living quality of public of the whole
city.
In large range. the negative impact of traffic noise wNith JRR is less than that of without JRR:
the impact of vehicle emission on air environment is larger than the existing situation. but the
increasing rate is less than that of without JRR. Comiipared wvith the existing situation. the
increasing rate of air pollutants otfwith or without .IRR is shown in Table 7-1.
When the project is comnpletedl. the density of pollutants in the air at most road sections is
lower than that of vxithout .IRR.
Moving of' tram line w ill solke the problem of mLtuaLl interf'erenice of vehicles and tramcars.
'I'he interference occurs mainly in front of Anshan RailwaN Station. at Jianguo Road section

from Rainbovw Bridge to W\us i Road Iitersection aind at areai near Lishan Underpass. In the
meantime. the negative inmacit (it tramear noise oln thc residients along the line X-ill he
reduced.

7.3 Negative Impact
In construction phase, normal traveling of vehicle and pedestrians will be negatively impacted.
and the living of the residents near the construction site will also be affected.
The project will occupy 44350 m- cultivated land wnhich can never be restored, and 103231
m2 green area (among which 57.38% of trees to be cut down are over 25 years old) will be
destroyed.
When the project is completed, it is not convenient for the public to cross the street. Due to
increased vehicle flow and speed. the impact of traffic noise on buildings adjacent to the road
sides will be more serious than the existing situation.
The density of air pollutants in the area of Laodong Road xvill be higher than that of without
JRR in 2010.
The negative impact in the view of vibration, surface water and sunshine will not be greater
than that of without JRR, and the impact of solid waste disposal during construction phase on
environment is very little.
7.4 Mitigation Measures for Serious Impacts
7.4.1 Design Phase
*   Traffic light for pedestrians crossing street shall be added at the intersections where the
public crosses the street frequently. Traffic policeman box shall be added on Jianguo
Road section in front of gate of Sifangtai Fruit Wholesale Market where there is heavy
flow of customers and vehicles to facilitate the pedestrians crossing street and vehicles
turning left.
*   By many times of discussions and agreement with ARPO, Anshan Urban and
Countryside Planning Institute and Beijing Municipal Project Design & Research
Institute, two sound barriers 3 m high and 250 m long shall be installed respectivelv on
the both sides of approach of Wuyi Road Interchange's section near Wuyi Road Primary
School.
* 91 air-conditioners shall be installed in the patient w%ard and diagnosis room of three
hospitals such as Hospital of Grain Bureau etc.: 262 air conditions shall be installed in
136



Liaoning Urban Transport Project-Anshan Subproject          Environmental Impact Assessment
the classrooms of 5 schools neighboring the project road; 5094 air-conditioners shall be
installed in the residential buildings neighboring the project road in order to reduce noise
pollution in summer when the windows open for ventilation.
* By agreement with the design institution, the original space of 5 m between the trees on
both sides of the street shall be changed to 2.5 m, in order to restore the green area
destroyed by the project as soon as possible. In 2010 all the destroyed green area can be
restored.
7.4.2 Construction Phase
APRO must clarify the environmental protection responsibility during the construction and
transportation while vntrusting the contractor with the project and must incorporate the
responsibility in the contract.
The construction shall be accomplished section by section and half by half at main places
such as AISC entrance; temporary passageways shall be set up during construction phase.
Designated person shall fetch pupils to cross the street when construction is being made near
schools.
The construction time shall be shortened; construction at night shall be avoided; construction
equipment and facilities of lower noise shall be used; operation at night of machinery with
high noise and vibration must be approved by Anshan Environment Protection Bureau.
By bulk transportation, the material must be covered and the transportation should avoid peak
hours of traffic; water sprinkling times should be added on the way; the site of construction
should have temporary store houses for bulk material; when old buildings or structures are
dismantled, plastic fence should be set up around building in order to suppress dust emission
to the environment.
In construction phase, Anshan Environmental Monitoring Center must carry Out monitoring
of noise, air, surface water and so on during construction phase.
7.4.3 Operational Phase
Anshan City has solemnly promised to develop and implement motor vehicle emission
control strategy (MVECS) to avoid deterioration of environment resulting from increase of
vehicles after 2010.
According to the traffic control program of the project. traveling of vehicles of extra large
size on the road must be restricted and the vehicle speed at night must be limited.
According to national technical strategy. lead-free petrol for vehicles should be soon applied
in the whole country before 2000: clean energy will be spread progressively; vehicles of high
pollution shall be eliminated: public traffic will be further developed; in proper time. the
existing tramcar line shall be partially changed into subw-ay and the whole line into light
tracks.
Vehicles must be inspected annually and randomly: the vehicles of high noise and emission
137



Liaoning Utrban Transport Project-Anslian Subproject   Environmental Impact Assessment
which are beyond standard m11USt be brought unlder control within the specified time. The
vehicles of high noise and emission which are beyond standard must not run.
Anshan Enxironmental l\onitorino Center will car-r out monitoring of noise. air. vibration
and surface water related to the project.
The city arrangement program must be improved fwLTher: the buildings adjacent to roadsides
will not be used as residence. school or hospital.
7.4.4 Summary
By many discussions with ARPO and design institute. the above mentioned mitigation have
been included in the &esign documents: During construction and operational phases, ARPO
will carry out concrete execution of the above mentioned mitigation measures. Since the
mitigation measures are favorable to protect Anshan urban environment, suppress
environmental further deterioration, they are feasible to be realized. After the mitigation
measures have been put into effect. the environment quality along the road will be
accordingly improved and the negative impact on the public will be reduced to a certain
extent.
Two public investigations have been carried out in EIA. The second social investigation to
the public demonstrates that 97.8% of 456 persons including peddlers to be moved from
Yongchang Market to Sandao Street Market think the impact of the project on them will be
reduced to the acceptable degree if the mitigation measures are executed. The other 2.2%
express indifferent attitude to the mitigation measures.
Anshan Environment Monitoring Center who will carry out environmental monitoring and
vehicle inspecting of this project is one of the best environmental organization with rich
experience and modem equipment in Liaoning Province and is able to complete the above
mentioned work. By consultation with Anshan municipal government, the environmental
administrative organization recommended in EIA report during construction and operational
phase is feasible.
7.5 Recommended Alternatives
Because the alternative B (the existing Shahe Street substitutes for Hebei Road construction)
has remarkable environmental profit in reducing occupation of cultivated land and avoiding
displacement of Shahe Village residents, it is recommended by EIA report. Since the negative
impact on environment of other alternatives is larger than or equal to that of the preferred
alignment, other alternatives are not recommended.
7.6 SUMMARY OF ASSESSMENT CONCLUSION
Based on achievement in different topics, the EIA report recognizes that the positive impact
on environment of JRR project is greater than the negative one. The project has reasonable
effect to improve environmental quality of Anshan City. The selected alignment of the project
is reasonable, the prc.,Tct is feasible from the view of environmental protection.

Annex 3:
LIAONING URBAN TRANSPORT PROJECT
OUTLINE OF TECHNICAL ASSISTANCE
FOR DEVELOPMENT OF MOTOR VEHICLE
EMISSION CONTROL STRATEGY
Draft
June 1998
Liaoning Urban Construction & Renewal Project Office
Post, Buckley International. Inc.
146



Liaoning Urban Transport Project-Anshan Subproject                    Environmental Impact Assessment
I Introduction
The implementation of Liaoning Urban Transport Project (LUTP) will result in increased traffic and motor
vehicle emissions, leading to deterioration of air quality along the project roads. Over the long term, the benefit
brought by the project on air quality from a city perspective will be offset by the expanded motor vehicle fleet.
Eventually, motor vehicle speeds on a city wide basis will slow down again and air quality in the project cities
will worsen. Although several quickly designed mitigation actions will be taken during the operation phase, they
are not able to fully address the fundamental cause of the long term air quality impact by the project due to the
complex nature of the issue.
The mitigation of the.long term project impacts on air quality and, ultimately, sustained improvement of air
quality in the project cities call for a well researched and structured motor vehicle emission control strategy
(MVECS). The MVECS is to provide the accurate assessment of present situation on motor vehicle emissions in
the projects cities as well as the trends in the future. Best available motor vehicle emission technologies and
successful experience in control motor vehicle emissions at home and from abroad will be evaluated for their
potential application in the project cities. On this basis, the MVECS will specify a series of effective, site
specific, integrated and goal oriented control, mitigation and remediation measures to tackle the long term
impact of the project on air quality.
Major efforts will be required in developing MVECS for each of the three project cities. A technical assistance is
therefore needed for necessary and appropriate technical and financial resources. This document outlines the
main scope and key elements in the proposed TA, including responsible organizations, the means of TA, the
contents of TA, estimated costs for the TA and the TA implementation.
2 The Responsible Organizations
LUCRPO and project offices in each city will be respo-sible for the implementation of this strategy. A capable
and experienced institute will be responsible for overal! integration. Local and foreign experts will be recruited
as consultants. One research institute in each city will be needed to be responsible for the strategy development,
and this institute will be selected in accordance with certain procedures based on the TOR.
3 Means of Technical Assistance
3.1 Consulting Services
Consultants experienced with motor vehicle emission reduction will be retained. The lead consultant will be
responsible for development of MVECS. and supported by research institutes from Shenyang, Anshan and
Fushun which are most familiar with motor vehicle fleet, air quality, urban and industrial development and local
policies in air quality control and environmental protection in general in their respective cities.
Since the local teams are limited b, their experience in dealing with complicated strategies for motor vehicle
emission control and latest development in motor emission control technologies, out-of-province consultants
who are with these experience will be retained to provide assistance and -uidance in MVECS development.
147



Liaoning tUrban Transport Project-Anshan Subproject                  Environmental Impact Assessment
3.2 Technical Workshop
A technical workshop wvill be held at the kex stage of the MVECS development. At the workshop. the local and
out-off-province consultants * ill present the findings from their initial study on the present motor vehicle issues
in the project cities. trends in the future in motor vehicle fleet and emissions. current mitigation measures and
their effectiveness. and local regulatorn framework related to air qualitN in general and motor vehicle emission in
specific.
Leading experts in this area will be invited to participate in the %%orkshop primarily those from cities which have
successfully developed and implemented an MVECS and improved their air quality because of it. The expens
are to provide their views and recommendations on the problems presented to them and share their successes and
learn from their lessons.
The objectives of the workshop will be exchange ideas, focusing on the specific issues facing the project cities.
The workshop will be organized as such that various motor vehicle emission control measures will be discussed
and debated for their effectiveness in addressing the motor vehicle emissions and air quality issues unique to
each of the project cities.
3.3 Overseas Study and Inspection
The provincial consultants as well as officials from the project cities responsible for developing, adoption and
implementing the MVECS will travel aboard to study similar MVECS in countries such as the US or Canada.
The study and inspection tour will be in cities which already have include meetings with MVECS development
and implementing agencies, MVECS facilities, institutes or companies involved in motor vehicle emission
control technology research and application, and regulatory agencies directly' relevant to air quality control.
particularly motor vehicle emission control.
4 Contents of Technical Assistance
4.1 lhformation collection and current situation assessment
Information on the present situation on motor vehicle emissions in each of the project cites will be collected and
compiled. Assessment of the collected information will be made to produce a clear and full understanding of
various aspects of the motor vehicle emission issue and its relation to air quality.
4.2 Research of the trends of the future
Future trends on the motor vehicle fleet, emission control technologies and other factors which may affect the
growth of motor vehicles such as population, urban development and standard of living in the future will be
researched. The objectives are to predict the variation in motor vehicle emissions, air pollution load, and air
quality in the future in the project cities.
148



Liaoning Urban Transport Project-Anshan Subproject                    E.avironmental Impact Assessment
4.3 Study of advanced motor vehicle control technologies and programs
Various technologies in motor vehicle emission control and reduction will be studied. The focus will be on their
effectiveness and success in application.
4.4 Development control measures
On the basis of a clear understandin2 of the issues facing the project cities, the trends of motor vehicle growth
and impact of the emissions on air quality. and knowledge of motor vehicle emission control technologies and
programs, a series of motor vehicle control measures will be developed as the core of the strategy. These
measures will include. bilt not be limited to:
stringent motor vehicle emission control standard and regulations:
promote unleaded fuel;
vehicle inspection and maintenance program:
catalytic purification facilities;
engine improvement;
retirement of aged vehicles;
monitor and enforcing the motor vehicle emission standards;
promote public transportation;
increase motor vehicle speeds;
motor vehicle quantity control in urban centers; and
develop clean or alternative fuel technologies.
4.5 Establishment of the implementing details
A detailed plan will be developed to ensure the strategy will be adopted and implemented. The details may
include designate executing/responsible agencies. implementing schedule, budget allocation, monitoring and
reporting procedures, and feedback system.
4.6 Reporting
A report will be prepared as the deliverable from the consultants for developing the MVECS. While in a single
volume. the report will cover all three project cities and specifv. where appropriate, the unique measures and
policies for each of the project cities. The report will provide full details of the MVECS and can be readily used
as guide for strategy implementation and progress monitoring by relevant organizations.
5 Costs and Implementation
5.1 Cost

presented in the following table. It shoUld be pointed out that more retined cost for the TA will be developed
when a full terms of reference for MV':CS development is prepared.
